Tayammum for Building Prayer When Fearing Loss of Eid Prayer
Ruling and disagreement on tayammum for building upon the Eid prayer when fearing loss.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tayammum for building upon the Eid prayer when hadath occurs, and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted for building on the Eid prayer if fearing loss due to crowd: Abu Hanifa permits; Sahibayn require risk of time expiry.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling from the chapter of taharah: the permissibility of tayammum to build upon a prayer when one has hadath and fears missing the Eid prayer. The Hanafi school is divided internally (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) and externally (vs. Shafi'i). Understanding the reasoning—istihsan based on fear of irreversible loss—is key to appreciating the school's methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Describe the situation: a person begins the Eid prayer with wudu, then has a hadath, and fears that performing wudu will cause him to miss the prayer entirely.
The fear is not just of time passing but of losing the congregational aspect of Eid prayer.
2
State the agreed upon rulings
Note the scenarios where all three Hanafi imams agree: if the person can catch part of the prayer with the imam, he must do wudu; if he fears the sun will set, tayammum is permitted.
These agreements set the boundary for the dispute.
3
Locate the dispute
Identify the disputed scenario: when there is neither fear of time expiring nor hope of catching the imam. Here, Abu Hanifa permits tayammum; the Sahibayn do not.
The Sahibayn argue that the latecomer can pray after the imam, so no fear of loss.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa considers the crowd on Eid day: if prayed alone, an obstacle may invalidate the prayer, so fear of loss remains. This is an istihsan based on potential harm.
He weighs the possibility of invalidation against the strict requirement of wudu.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i does not permit tayammum for Eid or funeral prayers because they can be repeated, so there is no irreversible loss.
This highlights the Hanafi concept of 'fawt ma yafūtu lā ilā khalaf' (loss of something without replacement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة التيمم
وبعد الشروع متوضئاً والحدث للبناء جاز له أن يتيمم ويشرع فيها ، هذا بالاتفاق ، وبعد الشروع متوضئاً والحدث للبناء) : أي إذا شرع " في صلاة العيدِ مُتَوضُناً، ثم سبقه الحدث، ويخافُ أنه إن توضأ تفوتُهُ الصَّلاةُ جاز له أن يتيمم للبناء، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له خلافاً لهما، وإن شرعَ بالتيمم، وسبقَهُ الحدثُ جَازَ لَهُ التَّيمم للبناء بالاتفاق. ذلك يدلّ على جواز التيمم لخوف فوت ما يفوت لا إلى خلف، وقد بسطنا كل ذلك في السعابيه[؟]». قوله : بالاتفاق ... الخ ؛ أي بين أئمتنا الثلاثة خلافاً للشافعي ، فإنه لم يجوز التيمم لصلاة العيد ولا صلاة الجنازة، بمجرد خوفِ الفوت بناءً على أنه يجوز إعادتهما، فلا يتحقق فيهما الفوت لا إلى خلف. قوله : أي إذا شرع ... الخ ؛ توضيحه : أنه إذا شرع في صلاة العيد بالوضوء، وسبقه الحدث في خلال الصلاة، فإن كان لا يخافُ ذهاب الوقتِ ويمكنه أن يدرك شيئاً منها مع الإمام توضأ ولا يتيمم اتفاقاً ؛ لإمكان أداء الباقـي بعــده ، وإن خاف زوال الشمس لو اشتغل بالوضوء يُباح له التيمم اتفاقاً. ولو لم يخف زوال الشمس ولا رجاء إدراكهما مع الإمام، فعنده يتيمم ويبني خلافاً لهما ؛ لأن اللاحق يصلّي بعد فراغ الإمام من صلاته، فلا يخاف الفوت؛ لأنه في حكم الصلاة بالجماعة، وأبو حنيفة الله[؟] نظر إلى أنَّ يوم العيد يوم زحمة، فلعله يعرضُهُ عارض يفسد صلاته إذا صلّى منفرداً فخوف الفوتِ في حقه باق، فلذلك أباح التيمم للبناء). كذا في «الهداية»، وحواشيها. قوله : جاز له التيمم ؛ لأنا لو أوجبنا عليه الوضوء يكون واجداً للماء في صلاته، فتفسد صلاته، فإنّ المتيمم إذا وجد الماء في خلال صلاته يجب عليه أن يستأنف الصلاة.
Book of Purification - Tayammum. And after beginning in a state of wudu and (then) the hadath (occurs) for building (upon the prayer), it is permissible for him to perform tayammum and begin (the prayer). This is by agreement. "And after beginning in a state of wudu and the hadath for building" means: if he begins the Eid prayer in a state of wudu, then the hadath overtakes him, and he fears that if he performs wudu the prayer will escape him, it is permissible for him to perform tayammum for building. This is according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (the two disciples). And if he begins with tayammum and the hadath overtakes him, it is permissible for him to perform tayammum for building by agreement. That indicates the permissibility of tayammum due to fear of losing what is lost without return (i.e., prayer cannot be repeated). And we have elaborated all that in Al-Sa'ayah. He said: "By agreement" means among our three imams, contrary to Al-Shafi'i, for he did not permit tayammum for the Eid prayer nor the funeral prayer merely due to fear of loss, based on that both can be repeated, so there is no loss without return. He said: "If he begins" ... its clarification: if he begins the Eid prayer with wudu, and the hadath overtakes him during the prayer, then if he does not fear the passing of time and can catch part of it with the imam, he performs wudu and does not perform tayammum by agreement, because it is possible to perform the remainder after that. And if he fears the setting of the sun if he busies himself with wudu, tayammum is permitted for him by agreement. And if he neither fears the setting of the sun nor hopes to catch them (the imams?) with the imam, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) he performs tayammum and builds, contrary to them (the two disciples), because the latecomer prays after the imam finishes his prayer, so he does not fear loss, because he is in the ruling of congregational prayer. Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) considered that the day of Eid is a crowded day, perhaps an obstacle will occur that invalidates his prayer if he prays alone, so the fear of loss remains in his case, therefore he permitted tayammum for building. Thus in Al-Hidayah and its glosses. He said: "He is permitted tayammum" because if we obligated wudu upon him, he would be one who finds water during his prayer, so his prayer would become invalid, for the one who performs tayammum, if he finds water during his prayer, he must restart the prayer.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn regarding tayammum for building (al-bina') upon a prayer when one fears missing the Eid prayer. The author begins by stating the ruling: if one starts the Eid prayer with wudu and then has a hadath, and fears that if he performs wudu the prayer will be lost, it is permissible for him to perform tayammum and build upon his prayer. This is the position of Abu Hanifa. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa's two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), disagree. The commentary then explains that if one starts with tayammum and then has a hadath, tayammum for building is permissible by agreement among the three Hanafi imams. The author then clarifies that 'by agreement' means among the Hanafi imams, but Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees entirely: he does not permit tayammum for either Eid or funeral prayer out of fear of missing them, because he holds that these prayers can be repeated, so there is no irreversible loss. The commentary then elaborates on the scenario: if one starts the Eid prayer with wudu and the hadath occurs, three situations arise: (1) if he does not fear the time will expire and can catch part of the prayer with the imam, he must perform wudu by agreement; (2) if he fears the sun will set if he does wudu, tayammum is permitted by agreement; (3) if he neither fears the time passing nor hopes to catch the imam (i.e., the imam will finish before he can rejoin), then Abu Hanifa permits tayammum while the Sahibayn do not, arguing that the latecomer prays after the imam and thus does not fear loss since he is still in the ruling of jama'ah. Abu Hanifa, however, considers the crowd on Eid day: if he prays alone, something may occur that invalidates his prayer, so fear of loss remains. The commentary ends by explaining that if we obligated wudu, the person would be a finder of water during his prayer, invalidating it, since a mutayammim who finds water during prayer must restart.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl, performed when water is unavailable or its use would cause harm.
البناء (al-binā'): Building upon a validly begun prayer by continuing after a hadath, using tayammum instead of restarting.
صلاة العيد (salāt al-‘īd): The special congregational prayer performed on the two Eids (al-Fiṭr and al-Aḍḥā), which is considered wājib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the primary reason for permitting tayammum to build upon the Eid prayer when one has hadath?
A) The water is not available at all.
B) The fear of missing the prayer during the crowded Eid day.
C) The hadath is minor and does not require wudu.
D) The imam allows it for ease.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi position permits tayammum for building on the Eid prayer if one fears missing it due to crowd, based on istihsan for irreversible loss.

Rulings of Tayammum: Two Strikes and Full Coverage
States the ruling of tayammum: two strikes, order not required, isti'ab required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of strikes in tayammum and explain why full coverage (isti'ab) is required for validity.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires full coverage of face and hands; order between face and hands is not obligatory.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah clarifies two key aspects of tayammum: the number of strikes and the requirement of full coverage. The Hanafi school, based on the apparent meaning of the Quran and hadith, holds that order is not compulsory but full coverage is essential. Understanding these conditions ensures proper performance of tayammum when water is unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic actions of tayammum
According to the text, what are the required striking motions? (face wipe, hands to elbows). The text states: 'to wipe his face, and a strike for his hands with the elbows.'
2
Analyze the requirement of order (tartib)
The text states that order is not obligatory. How does the commentator prove this? He points to the use of the waw (and) which indicates mere conjunction, not sequence. Order is only recommended (sunnah).
3
Understand the condition of full coverage (isti'ab)
The fatwa requires complete wiping of the face and hands. What evidence supports this? The commentator says 'acting upon the apparent meaning of the Qur'an and ahadith.' The Qur'anic verse commands 'fa-m-sahu bi-wujuhikum wa-aydikum' which implies full wiping.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some narrations from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) say majority suffices, but the relied-upon position is full coverage.
4
Apply the rule to edge cases
The text gives practical examples: moving a tight ring, removing a bracelet, separating fingers—all to ensure dust reaches the skin. These illustrate that any barrier invalidates tayammum unless moved.
5
Address the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text says 'al-asahh huwa al-isti'ab' (the more correct is full coverage) in contrast to the narration from al-Hasan. This tarjih is based on the apparent meaning of the primary texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لمسح وجهه، وضربة ليديه مع مرفقيه) ، ولا يشترط" الترتيب عندنا، والفتوى على أنه يشترط الاستيعاب حتى لو بقي شيء قليل لا يجزئه . [1] قوله : لمسح وجهه ؛ فيه إشارة إلى أن المقصود من الضرب هو المسح ، فلو حصل بدونه كفى، كما لو أدخل رأسه في موضع الغبارِ بنية التيمم، ولو انهدم الحائط وظهر الغبار فحرَّك رأسه ونوى التيمم جاز. كذا في «الخلاصة». [2] قوله : ولا يشترط ؛ فيه إشارة إلى سرِّ عطف الضربة الثانية على الأولى في المتن بالواو التي تدل على مطلق الجمعية، وإلى أن الترتيب بتقديم مسح الوجه مسنون كما أشار إليه في المتن بتقديمه ذكراً. [3]قوله : والفتوى ؛ مقابلة أنَّ الأكثرَ كافٍ كما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة الا الله ، وإنما كان الأصح هو الاستيعاب (۱) ، عملاً بظاهر القرآن والأحاديث. [4] قوله : لا يجزئه ؛ فيجب أن يمسح ما تحت الحاجبين فوق العينين، كما في «المحيط»(۲)، ومسح العذار، كما في «القنية»، ولو لم يحرِّك الخاتم إن كان ضيقاً، وكذا المرأة إن لم تحرّك السوار لم يجز، كما في «الخانية»، و«الولوالجيّة»، ويجب تخليل الأصابع، كما في «المنية».
To wipe his face, and a strike for his hands with the elbows, and order is not required according to us, and the fatwa is that full coverage is required such that if even a little remains, it does not suffice. [1] He said: 'to wipe his face' – therein is an indication that the purpose of the strike is wiping, so if wiping occurs without striking, it suffices, as if he inserted his head into a dusty place with the intention of tayammum, or if a wall collapsed and dust appeared, and he moved his head and intended tayammum, it is permissible. Likewise in al-Khulasah. [2] He said: 'and it is not required' – therein is an indication of the secret of connecting the second strike to the first in the text with the waw which indicates mere conjunction, and that order by preceding the wiping of the face is sunnah as indicated by the text by mentioning it first. [3] He said: 'and the fatwa' – in contrast to that the majority is sufficient as narrated by al-Hasan from Abu Hanifah, but the more correct is full coverage, acting upon the apparent meaning of the Qur'an and ahadith. [4] He said: 'it does not suffice' – so it is obligatory to wipe what is under the eyebrows above the eyes, as in al-Muhit, and to wipe the cheek, as in al-Qunyah, and if he does not move the ring if it is tight, and likewise the woman if she does not move the bracelet, it is not valid, as in al-Khaniyyah and al-Walwaljiyyah, and it is obligatory to separate the fingers, as in al-Munyah.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil) from the commentary on al-Wiqayah. It states the basic action of tayammum: one strike to wipe the face, and one strike for the hands up to the elbows. The Hanafi school holds that order (tartib) between these two strikes is not obligatory, contrary to some others. However, the relied-upon position (fatwa) is that full coverage (isti'ab) of the face and hands is required; any uncovered area invalidates the tayammum. The commentator explains that the word 'strike' (ضرب) is used to indicate that the intent is to obtain dust, but if dust reaches the face without striking (e.g., by putting the head in dust), it is valid. The use of 'waw' (and) between the two strikes shows order is not required, though it is recommended to start with the face. The proof for full coverage is the apparent meaning of the Qur'anic verse of tayammum and the hadiths. In practice, this means one must wipe the eyebrows, the cheeks (al-udhar), move a tight ring or bracelet, and separate the fingers to ensure dust reaches between them.

Key Terms
الاستيعاب (al-isti'ab): Full coverage of the limb with dust; no area left unwiped.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Performing the actions in a specific order (face before hands).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa in this text, what is required for the validity of tayammum?
A) Order between face and hands
B) Full coverage of the face and hands
C) Two strikes with a third if dust does not reach between fingers
D) Wiping only what is necessary for prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires full coverage (isti'ab) of face and hands in tayammum, but order (tartib) is only recommended, not obligatory.

Valid Earth for Tayammum: Definition and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Defines valid earth for tayammum and presents intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on wiping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'jins al-ard' and distinguish materials valid for tayammum, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding dust transfer during wiping.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid on any pure substance of the genus of earth—dust, sand, stone—but not on combustibles, metals, or food grains.

This passage establishes the foundational Hanafi rule that tayammum may be performed on any pure substance belonging to the 'genus of earth' (jins al-ard). The definition is broader than in other schools, including sand and stone alongside soil. The text also details the preferred method of wiping the forearms and highlights a significant internal disagreement: whether dust must actually reach the skin between the fingers. Understanding this distinction is critical for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the base rule for valid tayammum surfaces
Identify the opening phrase: 'on every pure substance from the genus of earth.' This is the general ruling.
The examples given are dust, sand, and stone.
2
Define 'jins al-ard' using the exclusion criteria
Apply al-Zayla`i's three exclusions: (1) anything that burns to ash, (2) anything that melts, (3) anything consumed by the earth (edible grains). Everything else is from the genus of earth.
Materials like wood, metals, and wheat are excluded.
3
Analyze the wiping method and the condition of dust
The best way to wipe uses specific fingers for each part of the forearm. There is a condition about dust entering between the fingers.
If dust does not reach, the text discusses the need for a third strike.
4
Differentiate between the two Hanafi positions
According to Imam Muhammad, tayammum is invalid without dust, so a third strike is needed if dust does not penetrate. According to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, dust penetration is not required; wiping suffices, and a third strike is unnecessary.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the latter, but avoiding used dust is recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على كل طاهر من جنس الأرض كالتراب، والرمل، والحَجَر والأحسن في مسح الذراعين أن يمسح ظاهرَ الدّراعِ اليُمْنى بالوسطى" والبنْصَر والخِنْصَرِ مع شيء من الكفّ اليسرى، مبتدئاً من رؤوس الأصابع، ثم باطنها بالمسبحة والإبهام إلى رؤوس الأصابع، وهكذا يفعلُ بالذراع اليُسرى. ثمَّ إذا لم يُدْخِلِ الغبار بين أصابعه، فعليه أن يخلل أصابعه، فيحتاج إلى ضربة ثالثة لتخليلها. [1] قوله : والأحسن ؛ إنما كان هذا الطريق أحسن ؛ لأنّ فيه تحرزاً عن استعمال التراب المستعمل، وهو وإن كان غير مضرِ ، فإنّ التراب لا يكون مستعملاً على الأصح ، لكن الاجتناب عنه أولى. [2]قوله : بالوسطى ... الخ ؛ هيا التي تلي المسبحة على خلاف جهة الإبهام، وما يليها بنصر بكسر الباء وسكون النون وفتح الصاد وما يليها وهو أصغر الأصابع خِنْصَر على وزن البنصر. [3] قوله : فيحتاج ؛ هذا على رواية محمد الله ؛ لأنَّ عنده لا يجوز التيمم بلا غبار، فحيث لم يصل الغبار بين الأصابع احتيج إلى ضربة أخرى، وأما عند غيره فلا يجب إيصال الغبار، بل يكفي المسح ، فيجب عليه التخليل، وإن لم يصل الغبار إليه من غير احتياج إلى ضربة ثالثة كذا في «الدر المختار وغيره. [4]قوله : من جنس الأرض ؛ الفارقُ بين ما هو جنس الأرض، وبين ما ليس من جنسه على ما ذكره الزَّيْلَعِي () أنّ كلَّ شيءٍ يحترقُ بالنار فيصير رماداً كالشجر والحطب ، وكل شيء يـلـيـن ويذوب بالنار كالحديد والذهب والفضة، وكل ما تأكله الأرض كالحنطة والشعير وسائر الحبوب ليس من جنس الأرض ، وما ليس كذلك فهو من جنس الأرض، فالقسم الأوّل لا يجوز عليه التيمم ما لم يكن عليه غبار يمسح وجهه
On every pure (substance) that is from the genus of earth, such as dust, sand, and stone. The best in wiping the forearms is to wipe the back of the right forearm with the middle finger, ring finger, little finger, and part of the left palm, starting from the fingertips, then the inner side with the index finger and thumb to the fingertips, and similarly for the left forearm. Then if dust does not enter between his fingers, he must separate his fingers, and needs a third strike to separate them. [1] He said: 'the best' – this way is best because it avoids using already used dust, and although used dust is not harmful (since dust is not considered 'used' according to the more correct view), refraining is better. [2] He said: 'with the middle finger...' – it is the one next to the index finger opposite the thumb, and what follows it is the 'binsir' (ring finger), and what follows it is the little finger. [3] He said: 'so he needs' – this is according to the narration of Muhammad (r.a.), because in his view tayammum is not valid without dust; so when dust does not reach between the fingers, another strike is needed. But according to others, it is not obligatory to make dust reach; rather wiping is sufficient, so he must separate his fingers even if dust does not reach them, without needing a third strike. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others. [4] He said: 'from the genus of earth' – the distinction between what is of the genus of earth and what is not, according to al-Zayla`i: everything that burns by fire and becomes ash, like wood and firewood, and everything that softens and melts by fire, like iron, gold, and silver, and everything that the earth consumes, like wheat, barley, and other grains, is not of the genus of earth. What is not like that is of the genus of earth. The first category is not permissible for tayammum unless there is dust on it with which to wipe his face.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling specifying the valid materials for tayammum. The base text states that tayammum is permissible on every pure substance that is from the genus of earth (jins al-ard), such as dust, sand, and stone. The commentator explains that 'earth' here excludes things that burn to ash (wood), melt (metals), or are consumed by the earth (grains). Only substances that do not have these properties are considered from the genus of earth. The text also provides the preferred method for wiping the forearms: using different fingers to cover both the back and inner sides, starting from the fingertips. A significant point of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is noted: according to Imam Muhammad (via his narration), tayammum requires dust to actually reach the skin; if it does not, an additional strike is needed. But according to the other two (Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf?), it is sufficient just to wipe without requiring dust to penetrate, though separating the fingers is still obligatory even without a third strike. This distinction affects the number of strikes in practice.

Key Terms
جنس الأرض (jins al-ard): The genus of earth: substances that do not burn to ash, do not melt, and are not consumed by the earth (e.g., sand, stone, dust).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following materials is NOT considered from the genus of earth (jins al-ard)?
A) Sand
B) Stone
C) Wood that turns to ash when burned
D) Dry soil

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid on any pure substance of the genus of earth (excluding combustibles, metals, and edibles), and the mufta bihi position does not require dust to penetrate between fingers.

Recommended Method of Wiping Forearms in Tayammum
Recommended forearm wiping method and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the preferred Hanafi method for wiping forearms in tayammum and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the need for a third strike for takhlil.

Core Idea
The best forearm wiping method avoids reused dust; a third strike is only required by Imam Muhammad.

In this passage, the commentator on Al-Wiqayah explains the optimal method (al-aḥsan) for wiping the forearms during tayammum. The method is designed to avoid using dust that has already been applied, even though Hanafis hold that dust does not become 'used' like water. The passage also highlights a key difference within the school: while Imam Muhammad requires a third strike if dust does not penetrate between the fingers, the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) considers takhlil sufficient without a third strike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred method
The passage states that the best way is to wipe the outer right forearm with the left palm using specific fingers, starting from fingertips, then inner side with index and thumb. Repeat for left arm.
This method avoids using dust that may have been previously applied.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains this method is 'aḥsan' because it avoids using 'used dust' (turāb musta‘mal), even though the correct view is that dust does not become used.
Avoidance is still preferable.
3
Define takhlīl and its occasion
If dust does not naturally enter between the fingers, one must perform takhlīl (passing fingers of one hand through the other) to ensure dust reaches.
This is wajib (obligatory) according to all Hanafi imams.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf
Imam Muhammad holds that a third strike (ḍarbah thālithah) is required for takhlīl because he considers dust essential for valid tayammum. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the initial two strikes suffice; takhlīl can be done without a third strike.
This difference stems from the necessity of visible dust.
5
Determine the muftā bihī
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no third strike needed, only takhlīl.
Cited from al-Durr al-Mukhtār.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأحسن في مسح الذراعين أن يمسح ظاهرَ الذراعِ اليُمْنَى بالوسطى والبنصر والخِنصر مع شيء من الكف اليُسرى، مبتدئاً من رؤوس الأصابع، ثم باطنها بالمسبحة والإبهام إلى رؤوس الأصابع، وهكذا يفعل بالذراع اليُسرى. ثم إذا لم يُدْخِلِ الغبار بين أصابعه، فعليه أن يخلل أصابعه، فيحتاج إلى ضربة ثالثة لتخليلها. [1] قوله : والأحسن؛ إنما كان هذا الطريق أحسن؛ لأن فيه تحرزاً عن استعمال التراب المستعمل، وهو وإن كان غير مضر؛ فإن التراب لا يكون مستعملاً على الأصح، لكن الاجتناب عنه أولى. [2] قوله : بالوسطى ... الخ؛ هي التي تلي المسبحة على خلاف جهة الإبهام، وما يليها بنصر بكسر الباء وسكون النون وفتح الصاد وما يليها وهو أصغر الأصابع خِنصر على وزن البنصر. [3] قوله : فيحتاج؛ هذا على رواية محمد رحمه الله؛ لأن عنده لا يجوز التيمم بلا غبار، فحيث لم يصل الغبار بين الأصابع احتيج إلى ضربة أخرى، وأما عند غيره فلا يجب إيصال الغبار، بل يكفي المسح، فيجب عليه التخليل، وإن لم يصل الغبار إليه من غير احتياج إلى ضربة ثالثة كذا في «الدر المختار» وغيره.
And the best [way] in wiping the forearms is that he wipes the outer side of the right forearm with the middle finger, ring finger, and little finger along with some of the left palm, starting from the tips of the fingers, then its inner side with the index finger and thumb to the tips of the fingers, and similarly he does with the left forearm. Then if the dust did not enter between his fingers, he must do takhlil (passing fingers through each other) of his fingers, so he needs a third strike for takhlil. [1] He said: 'And the best' – this way is best because it avoids using used dust, and although it is not harmful (since dust is not considered used according to the most correct view), avoiding it is better. [2] He said: 'with the middle finger... etc.' – it is the one that follows the index finger on the side opposite the thumb, and what follows it is the ring finger (binṣir, with kasra on bā', sukūn on nūn, fatḥa on ṣād), and what follows it is the little finger (khinṣir, on the pattern of binṣir). [3] He said: 'so he needs' – this is according to the riwāyah of Muḥammad (raḥimahullāh), because according to him tayammum is not valid without dust, so when dust did not reach between the fingers, a third strike is needed. But according to others, it is not obligatory to make the dust reach; rather wiping is sufficient, so he must do takhlīl even if dust does not reach it without needing a third strike, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtār and others.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement describing the optimal method (al-aḥsan) for wiping the forearms in tayammum. The annotator (Ṣāḥib al-‘Umda) expands on the base text by explaining why this method is preferred: it avoids using dust that has already been applied (al-turāb al-musta‘mal). Although the stronger opinion is that dust does not become 'used' (like water in wudū’), avoidance is better. The passage then details the finger names and the positions. A key point is that if dust does not penetrate between the fingers, one must do takhlīl (interlacing fingers). According to Imām Muḥammad (raḥimahullāh), a third strike is required because tayammum without dust is invalid in his view. However, according to Abū Ḥanīfah and Abū Yūsuf, the mere wiping suffices even without visible dust; thus takhlīl is obligatory but a third strike is not needed. The relied-upon position (al-muftā bihī) is that of Abū Ḥanīfah and Abū Yūsuf, as mentioned in al-Durr al-Mukhtār.

Key Terms
تخليل (takhliīl): Passing the fingers of one hand through the fingers of the other to ensure dust reaches between them.
ضربة ثالثة (ḍarbah thālithah): A third strike of the hands on earth for the purpose of takhlīl alone.
تراب مستعمل (turāb musta‘mal): Dust already applied to the limbs in tayammum, analogous to used water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the muftā bihī view in the Hanafī school, what is required if dust does not reach between the fingers during tayammum?
A) A third strike is required.
B) Takhlīl is required without a third strike.
C) The tayammum is invalid.
D) No action is needed.

Key Takeaway
The optimal method for wiping forearms in tayammum avoids reused dust, and the relied-upon Hanafi position does not require a third strike for takhlīl.

Definition of 'Genus of Earth' and Permissible Substances for Tayammum
Defines genus of earth and lists rulings for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'min jins al-ard' using the Hanafi three-part test and determine the validity of tayammum on a given substance.

Core Idea
A substance is from the genus of earth if it does not burn to ash, melt, or decay; tayammum is valid on it with or without dust.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies what makes a substance suitable for tayammum. The Hanafi school provides a clear, principled test to distinguish earth-like substances from others. Understanding this test is crucial for correctly applying tayammum when water is unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories that are NOT from the genus of earth
Everything that burns to ash (like wood), melts (like metals), or is consumed by earth (like grains) is excluded. Use this test to classify any substance.
The test is from al-Zayla‘ī and is unique to the Hanafī school.
2
Understand the dust (ghubār) requirement for non-earth substances
If a substance is not from the genus of earth, tayammum is only valid if sufficient dust (ghubār) is present on it to wipe the face and hands.
The dust must be actual earth dust, not just any powder.
3
Recognize the list of permissible earth-like substances
Many substances are explicitly listed as permissible even without dust: stone, baked brick, kohl, gypsum, coral, etc. Note the prohibition of pearl because it originates from water.
The list is not exhaustive; the test determines new cases.
4
Distinguish the special case of najāsah ḥukmiyyah
A place that had impurity but is now dry and clean is pure for prayer but NOT for tayammum. This is a unique Hanafī nuance: dryness purifies for prayer but not for the substitute ritual.
This explains why the author's general statement 'pure' needed qualification.
5
Note the implicit criticism of the matn and its resolution
The commentator points out that the base text's absolute use of 'pure' could be misleading. He promises to clarify later that purification by drying applies only to prayer, not tayammum.
This shows the commentator's role in refining the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على كل طاهر من جنس الأرض كالتراب، والرمل، والحجر... [4] قوله : من جنس الأرض؛ الفارقُ بين ما هو جنس الأرض، وبين ما ليس من جنسه على ما ذكره الزَّيْلَعِي () أنّ كلَّ شيءٍ يحترقُ بالنار فيصير رماداً كالشجر والحطب، وكل شيء يـلـيـن ويذوب بالنار كالحديد والذهب والفضة، وكل ما تأكله الأرض كالحنطة والشعير وسائر الحبوب ليس من جنس الأرض، وما ليس كذلك فهو من جنس الأرض، فالقسم الأوّل لا يجوز عليه التيمم ما لم يكن عليه غبار يمسح وجهه، وكذا الكحل والزرنيخ. وأما الذهب والفضة فلا يجوز بهما، إذا كانا مسبوكين، فإن كانا غير مسبوكين مختلطين بالتراب يجوز بهما. والحنطة والشعير إن كان عليهما غبار يجوز، وإلا فلا. ولا يجوز على مكان كان فيه نجاسة وقد زال أثرها، مع أنه يجوزُ الصَّلاةُ فيه ويديه به، والأوّل) يجوز التيمم به وإن لم يكن عليه غبار. [1] قوله : وكذا؛ أي يجوز التيمم بالكحل بالضم: سرمه، والزرنيخ : بكسر الزاي المعجمة، وسكون الراء المهملة، وكسر النون، وسكون الياء المثناة التحتية، بعدها فاء معجمة : هرتال وكذا يجوز بالجص والثورة والأرض السبخة، والمراد أسبخ، والأثمد والآجر والحصى والكيزان والحيطان، وبالعقيق والزَّبَرْجَد. كذا في فتاوى قاضي خان. ويجوز بالمرجان لا باللؤلؤ؛ لأنها خلقت من الماء. كذا في «البحر » ) ، و «النهر [2] قوله : يجوز؛ لتحقق المسح على التراب؛ فإنّ الغبار تراب رقيق، وكذا لو ضرب يده على الثوب أو اليد ولزق بيده التراب فتیمم به جاز. [3] قوله : ولا يجوز؛ فيه تعريض على المصنّف في إطلاقه الطاهر، فيلزم عليه أن يجوز التيمم بمثل هذا المكان؛ لكونه طاهراً حتى جازت الصلاة عليه، مع أنه لا يجوز، وكأنه إنما أطلق هاهنا اعتماداً على ما سيصرح به في باب الأنجاس أنَّ الأرض والآجر المفروش تطهر باليبس وذهاب الأثر للصلاة لا للتيمم، وسنذكر وجه الفرق بين جواز الصلاة وجواز التيمم هناك إن شاء الله تعالى.
On every pure thing from the genus of earth, like dust, sand, and stone... [4] He said: 'from the genus of earth' – the distinction between what is of the genus of earth and what is not, as mentioned by al-Zayla‘ī, is that everything that burns with fire and becomes ash, like trees and wood, and everything that softens and melts with fire, like iron, gold, and silver, and everything that the earth eats (decays), like wheat, barley, and all grains, is not of the genus of earth. And what is not like that is of the genus of earth. So the first category [those not of earth] is not permissible to perform tayammum on unless there is dust on it with which he wipes his face. Similarly, kohl and tutia [are permissible]. As for gold and silver, it is not permissible to perform tayammum on them if they are minted (cast). If they are not minted and mixed with dust, it is permissible. As for wheat and barley, if there is dust on them, it is permissible; otherwise not. And it is not permissible to perform tayammum on a place where there was impurity and its trace has disappeared, even though prayer is permissible in it and wiping on it [is allowed]? And the first [i.e., those of the genus of earth without dust] it is permissible to perform tayammum on even if there is no dust on it. [1] He said: 'Similarly' – meaning tayammum is permissible with kohl (antimony), tutia (zinc oxide), gypsum, clay, saline soil, stibnite, fired brick, pebbles, jugs (kīzān), walls, agate, and emerald. So in Fatāwā Qāḍī Khān. And it is permissible with coral but not with pearl because it is created from water. So in al-Baḥr and al-Nahr. [2] He said: 'it is permissible' – because wiping on dust is achieved; indeed dust is fine earth. Similarly, if he strikes his hand on a garment or hand and some dust sticks to his hand and he performs tayammum with it, it is permissible. [3] He said: 'and it is not permissible' – in this there is an implicit criticism of the author [al-Wiqāyah] because he used the word 'pure' absolutely, which would entail that tayammum is permissible on such a place because it is pure, even prayer is permissible on it, whereas it is not [permissible]. It is as if he only used it here relying on what he will clarify in the chapter on impurities: that the earth and fired bricks laid down become pure by drying and disappearance of the trace for prayer but not for tayammum. We will mention the difference between permissibility of prayer and permissibility of tayammum there, God willing.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling that clarifies the key condition for valid tayammum: the substance must be 'min jins al-ard' (from the genus of earth). The commentator, following al-Zayla‘ī, provides a practical test: anything that burns to ash (like wood), melts (like metals), or is eaten/decayed by earth (like grains) is NOT from the genus of earth. Thus, tayammum on these substances is only valid if they have dust (ghubār) on them that can be wiped. Substances that are earth-like but without dust (like stone or baked brick without dust) are permissible even without dust, as they are from the genus. The passage then lists specific items and their rulings: kohl (ithmid), tutia (zinc oxide), gypsum, saline soil, stibnite, fired brick, pebbles, jugs, walls, agate, emerald are all permissible. Coral is permissible but pearl is not because it originates from water (and thus is not earth-like). Gold and silver are not permissible if minted (masbūk) because they are metals; but if they are in dust form mixed with earth, they become permissible. Wheat and barley are permissible only if dust is on them; otherwise not. A crucial point is the distinction between a place that was najis but has become dry and clean: prayer is valid on it, but tayammum is not. This seems contradictory to the author's general statement 'pure', but the commentator explains that the author will later clarify that drying purifies for prayer but not for tayammum. The underlying wisdom is that tayammum requires actual earth (turāb), not mere dryness. The commentator also notes that if one strikes a garment or hand and obtains enough dust, tayammum is valid.

Key Terms
من جنس الأرض (min jins al-ard): Substances that share the earthy nature: do not burn to ash, do not melt, and are not consumed by the earth.
غبار (ghubār): Fine dust that can be wiped; it is necessary for tayammum on substances not of the genus of earth.
مسبوك (masbūk): Cast or minted metal (e.g., gold coins, silver bars). Tayammum is not valid on them.
نجاسة حكمية (najāsah ḥukmiyyah): An impurity whose physical trace has disappeared, but the place is considered pure only for prayer, not for tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī school, on which of the following is tayammum valid without any dust?
A) A wooden plank
B) A gold coin
C) A clean stone
D) Wheat grains

Key Takeaway
For tayammum to be valid, the substance must be from the genus of earth or have sufficient dust; a place that was impure but now dry is not valid for tayammum despite being pure for prayer.

Permissible Substances for Tayammum: Earth and Its Derivatives
Ruling on substances valid for tayammum and intra/inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which substances are valid for tayammum according to the Hanafi school and explain the dispute with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i regarding ash.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid on any pure substance from the genus of earth, but not on wood ash unless it originates from stone.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the Hanafi position on what constitutes 'pure earth' (sa'id) for tayammum. It lists a wide range of permissible substances and addresses a key dispute: whether ash from wood is valid. Understanding this dispute reveals how different interpretations of the Quran and hadith lead to different fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The Hanafi school defines 'sa'id' as any pure substance from the genus of earth (jins al-ard). List the examples given: soil, sand, stone, brick, etc.
The principle: 'al-ard kulluha sa'id'.
2
Note the exception for ash
Ash is invalid because it is from wood, not earth. But if ash comes from stone, it becomes permissible.
The comment on Turkestan stone ash.
3
Contrast with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i
They restrict tayammum to soil or sand only. Their proof is the hadith 'Made its soil pure for us' (Muslim).
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis rely on the Quranic verse 'sa'id' (4:43) and the general hadith 'the earth was made a mosque and purification'. They argue the narrow interpretation is unsupported by strong evidence.
The weak hadith 'Take to the earth' is criticized.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a piece of sun-dried brick, is tayammum valid? Yes, because it is from earth. Given wood ash, no.
Also consider surfaces with previous impurity: tayammum invalid even if dry.

ولا يجوز بالرماد هذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد . وأما عند أبي يوسف : فلا يجوز إلا بالتراب أو الرمل.
وعند الشافعي : لا يجوز إلا بالتراب.
قوله : ولا يجوز؛ لأن الرماد ليس من جنس الأرض، بل هو من جنس الشجر كما هو الغالب، فإن كان الرماد من حجر كما في بعض بلاد تركستان ؛ فإن الحجر حطبهم جاز التيمم به ، كما في «جامع الرموز» نقلاً عن «الخزانة».

Commentary: 'It is not permissible except with soil' due to the hadith: 'Made its soil – i.e., the earth – pure for us,' narrated by Muslim, Ibn Khuzayma, Ibn Hibban, and others. Abu Yusuf relied on it for its permissibility with sand. And it is the old view of al-Shafi'i, based on what was narrated by Ahmad, al-Bayhaqi, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Abu Ya'la and others from Abu Hurayra that some people from the desert came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: We stay in the sands for three or four months, and among us are the junub, menstruating, and postpartum women, and we do not find water. He said: 'Take to the earth.' But its chain is weak. The basis of Abu Hanifa and others for its permissibility with everything that is from the genus of pure earth is His saying: '...so perform tayammum with pure earth' (4:43), for it is interpreted as pure earth; and the hadiths that came with the wording: 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a means of purification,' and this is the strongest of the schools, and we have elaborated its proofs in al-Si'aya.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on al-Wiqaya discussing the substances permissible for tayammum. It begins by listing various substances like kohl, zinc, gypsum, chalk, salty soil, antimony, brick, pebbles, and even coral (but not pearls, as they are created from water). The author explains that any substance that is from the genus of earth (jins al-ard) is permissible, provided it is pure. Notably, the commentary clarifies that even if the substance lacks dust (ghubar), such as a hard stone, it is still valid for tayammum because the key is that it is earth-like. The passage then addresses a potential contradiction: if a place previously had najasa but is now pure by drying (e.g., brick), prayer is permissible there, but tayammum is not. The reason is that tayammum requires a purifying earth that can be wiped onto the limbs, not merely a purified surface. The main dispute concerns ash (ramad). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, tayammum with ash is invalid because ash is from the genus of wood, not earth. However, if the ash originates from stone (as in Turkestan where stone is used for fire), then it becomes permissible because stone is from the genus of earth. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold a stricter view: only pure soil (turab) or sand (raml) is permissible. Abu Yusuf supported his view with the hadith 'Made its soil pure for us,' while the Hanafi school's primary proof is the Quranic verse 'so perform tayammum with pure earth' (4:43), interpreting 'sa'id' as pure earth in a broad sense. The author notes that the strongest opinion (aqwa al-madhahib) is the Hanafi position, and he refers to his own work al-Si'aya for a detailed exposition of proofs.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): The surface of the earth; interpreted by the Hanafis as pure earth, including soil, sand, stone, brick, and other earth-like substances.
تراب (turab): Soil or dust; specifically, the finely ground particles of earth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The hadith specifically permits coral.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid on any pure substance from the genus of earth; ash from wood is invalid but from stone is valid due to origin.

Tayammum with Ash and Sand: Intra-Hanafi and Cross-Madhhab Differences
Ruling on tayammum with ash and sand with proofs and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on tayammum with different substances and evaluate the strength of the proofs.

Core Idea
Only what is from the genus of pure earth suffices for tayammum; ash from wood is not valid, ash from stone is.

This lesson examines the dispute within the Hanafi school and with the Shafi'i school regarding the validity of tayammum using ash and sand. We will trace the proofs and identify the relied-upon position, distinguishing between wood ash and stone ash.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on ash from wood vs stone
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, tayammum with wood ash is not valid because it is not from the genus of earth; stone ash is valid because stone is from the genus of earth.
This distinction is based on the origin of the ash.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf holds that tayammum is not valid with any ash at all, only with earth or sand.
Abu Yusuf's view is stricter within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the proof for the opposing view
The opposing view (Abu Yusuf and old Shafi'i) relies on a hadith about 'soil' being a purification, and a weak hadith about sand.
The commentator notes the weak chain of the sand hadith.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The preferred Hanafi view relies on the Quranic verse 'pure earth' (interpreted broadly) and the authentic hadith 'the earth was made for me a mosque and a purification'.
The general wording of these proofs supports the broader interpretation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (stone ash is valid; wood ash is not). The practical difference: Shafi'is restrict to pure soil, while Hanafis allow sand and stone ash.
This affects travelers in regions where stone is used as fuel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز بالرماد هذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وأما عند أبي يوسف فلا يجوز إلا بالتراب أو الرمل. وعند الشافعي لا يجوز إلا بالتراب. قوله ولا يجوز لأن الرماد ليس من جنس الأرض بل هو من جنس الشجر كما هو الغالب فإن كان الرماد من حجر كما في بعض بلاد تركستان فإن الحجر حطبهم جاز التيمم به كما في جامع الرموز نقلا عن الخزانة. قوله لا يجوز إلا بالتراب لحديث جعلت تربتها أي الأرض لنا طهورا أخرجه مسلم وابن خزيمة وابن حبان وغيرهم واستند أبو يوسف له في جوازه بالرمل وهو قول الشافعي له القديم بما أخرجه أحمد والبيهقي وإسحاق بن راهويه وأبو يعلى وغيرهم عن أبي هريرة أن ناسا من أهل البادية أتوا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالوا إنا نكون بالرمال الأشهر الثلاثة والأربعة ويكون فينا الجنب والحائض والنفساء ولا نجد الماء فقال عليكم بالأرض وسنده ضعيف. ومستند أبي حنيفة وغيره في جوازه بكل ما كان من جنس الأرض طاهر قوله فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا فإنه مفسر بالأرض الطاهرة والأحاديث التي وردت بلفظ جعلت لي الأرض مسجدا وطهورا وهذا أقوى المذاهب وقد بسطنا دلائلها في السعاية.
And it is not permissible with ashes. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. As for according to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible except with earth or sand. And according to Al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible except with earth. He said: 'And it is not permissible' because ash is not of the genus of earth, rather it is of the genus of wood, as is usual. If the ash is from stone, as in some regions of Turkestan where stone is their fuel, then tayammum with it is permissible, as in Jami' al-Rumuz, quoting from al-Khazinah. Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on tayammum with ashes and sand. It begins by stating the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad: tayammum with ashes is not valid. Then it mentions Imam Abu Yusuf's view that it is not valid except with earth or sand, meaning ashes are not permitted at all. The commentator explains that ash from wood is not from the genus of earth, so it is invalid. However, if the ash comes from stone (as in some regions where stone is used as fuel), then it is considered earth-like and tayammum with it is valid. The passage then presents the proof for Abu Yusuf's position, which is also the old view of Imam al-Shafi'i, based on a hadith about the earth being a purification. But the commentator notes that the chain of that hadith is weak. The preferred position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) relies on the Quranic verse 'so perform tayammum with pure earth' and the famous hadith 'the earth was made for me a mosque and a purification.' The commentator concludes that this is the strongest view and refers to his larger work al-Si'ayah for further evidence.

Key Terms
رماد (ramād): Ash from burning wood or other substances; not considered from the genus of earth unless from stone.
صعيد (ṣaʿīd): The surface of the earth, interpreted as pure earth that is not mixed with impurities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), is tayammum valid with ash from stone?
A) Yes, because stone is from the genus of earth.
B) No, ash from any source is invalid.
C) Only if no other medium is available.
D) Yes, but only according to Abu Yusuf.

Key Takeaway
In tayammum, only substances from the genus of pure earth are valid; wood ash is invalid, but sand and stone ash are valid according to the majority Hanafi view.

Is Dust Required for Tayammum? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on necessity of dust for tayammum with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the requirement of dust (ghubār) for tayammum, apply the Quranic evidence (dalil) used by each, and identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Dust is not required for tayammum – the earth itself suffices, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

You may have learned that tayammum requires striking pure earth and wiping your face and hands. But does that earth need to have visible dust? In this lesson, we examine an internal Hanafi disagreement: while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani permit tayammum even without dust, Abu Yusuf demands its presence. This dispute turns on how to interpret the Quranic phrase 'from it' (minhu) in verse 5:6. By the end, you will understand why the majority view prevails in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify which imams hold that dust is required and which do not. Note that the matn suggests validity without dust, and the commentator explains the ikhtilaf.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (one narration) say valid; Abu Yusuf and another narration from Muhammad say invalid without dust.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Analyze the Quranic verse (5:6) that Abu Yusuf uses: 'wipe your faces and your hands from it' (minhu). Explain how he argues that 'minhu' implies taking a part of the earth, which requires dust.
The pronoun 'hu' refers to the earth; transferring a part necessitates dust.
3
Examine the majority's proof
The majority rely on the general command to use 'pure earth' (ṣa‛īdan ṭayyiban) in another verse (4:43 or 5:6). They interpret 'minhu' as partitive only if dust is present; otherwise, the command is fulfilled by the earth itself.
The general command does not specify dust; dust is merely a fine form of earth.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The commentator states that the correct view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: tayammum is valid without dust absolutely. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Even according to this view, it is better to use dust if available, but it is not a condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو بلا نقع وعليه مع قدرته على الصعيد بنية أداء الصلاة [1]قوله ولو بلا نقع متعلق بالحجر أو بكل طاهر أي ولو كان ذلك الطاهر بلا نقع بالفتح أي غبار وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد له في رواية وفي رواية أخرى عنه وهو قول أبي يوسف الله أنه لا يجوز بدون الغبار لقوله فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُم مِّنْهُ فإن الضمير راجع إلى التراب فيقتضي ذلك استعمال جزء منه ولا يتصور ذلك بدون الغبار ومن لم يشترطه استند بقوله في موضع آخر فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا وفي المقام مباحث مذكورة في السعاية. [2]قوله مع قدرته على الصعيد إنما ذكره نفيا لما روي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا يجوز التيمم على الغبار نفسه إلا عند العجز عن الصعيد والصحيح قولهما أنه يجوز به مطلقا لأن الغبار تراب رقيق كذا في المحيط.
And [it is valid] even without dust, and upon him, while he is able to use pure earth, with the intention of performing prayer. [1] He said: 'And even without dust' is attached to 'stone' or 'every pure thing': i.e., even if that pure thing is without dust (with fatha, meaning ghubār). This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (in one narration), and in another narration from him, it is the saying of Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible without dust, due to His saying: 'So wipe your faces and your hands from it' (5:6). The pronoun refers to the earth, so it necessitates using a part of it, and that is not conceivable without dust. Whoever did not stipulate it relied on His saying in another place: 'So perform tayammum with pure earth.' There are investigations mentioned in al-Si'ayah. [2] He said: 'While he is able to use pure earth'; it is mentioned to negate what is reported from Abu Yusuf that tayammum on dust itself is not permissible except when unable to use pure earth. The correct view according to the two of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that it is permissible absolutely, because dust is fine earth. As in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement of dust (ghubār) for a valid tayammum. The matn says that tayammum is valid even without dust, but the commentary clarifies that this is only when the substance itself is from the genus of pure earth. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (in one narration), tayammum without dust is valid. However, in another narration from Muhammad and according to Abu Yusuf, tayammum is not valid without dust because the Quran says 'wipe your faces and your hands from it' – the pronoun 'it' refers to the earth, implying that some part of it must be used, which is only possible if there is dust. Those who do not require dust argue based on the general command to use pure earth. The commentator notes that the correct view according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that dust is not required; tayammum can be done on any pure earth even if no dust is raised, but if one is able to use pure earth, it is better to use dust. The commentator also mentions a related issue: Abu Yusuf reportedly held that tayammum on dust itself is only valid when unable to use pure earth, but the majority say it is valid absolutely because dust is fine earth.

Key Terms
نقع (naqʿ): Dust or fine particles that rise from the earth when struck or wiped.
غبار (ghubār): Fine particles of earth that can be seen and transferred.
صعيد (ṣaʿīd): Pure earth; the substance used for tayammum, including soil, sand, stone, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because dust is required.
B) Yes, because the majority do not require dust.
C) Only if one cannot find dusty earth.
D) No, because the Quran says 'from it'.

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view holds that dust (ghubār) is not a condition for valid tayammum; any pure earth suffices.

The Obligation of Intention (Niyyah) in Tayammum: Refuting Zufar's Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intention in tayammum; refutation of Zufar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention in tayammum, reconstruct Zufar's qiyas argument, and explain why the majority of Hanafis reject it using the principle that a substitute may differ from its original when evidence indicates.

Core Idea
A substitute can differ from its original when evidence dictates — intention is fard in tayammum, not wudu.

This passage addresses an internal Hanafi dispute: is intention (niyyah) obligatory in tayammum? Imam Zufar argued that since tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and wudu does not require intention (only sunnah), tayammum should also not require it. The commentator refutes this by establishing that it is permissible for a substitute to differ from its original when there is specific textual evidence. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, reinforces the core Hanafi position, and clarifies the distinction between wudu and tayammum regarding intention.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on intention in tayammum
Identify the ruling: intention (niyyah) is fard (obligatory) in tayammum, contrary to Zufar who says it is not fard.
The ruling applies to both adā' (timely) and qaḍā' (make-up) prayers.
2
Reconstruct Zufar's qiyas analogy
Map Zufar's argument: Asl (original) = wudu where intention is not fard; Far' (new) = tayammum; Illa (effective cause) = both are purifications, tayammum being a substitute; Hukm = intention not required.
Zufar's qiyas is jali (clear) analogical reasoning.
3
Identify the Hanafi response to Zufar
Understand that the majority Hanafis reject the qiyas because a substitute may differ from its original when evidence (dalīl) indicates. Here, the evidence from Quran and Sunnah establishes intention as fard in tayammum.
The principle is: 'lā ba'sa bi dhālika idhā dalla dalīl ʿalā mukhālafati al-khalaf li al-aṣl fī baʿḍi al-aḥkām'.
4
Formulate the correct principle
Generalise: a substitute does not have to mirror the original in all rulings; where specific evidence exists, the substitute can diverge. This is a key Hanafi usul principle.
This principle prevents mechanical qiyas from overriding explicit textual rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بنية أداء الصلاة [3]قوله أداء الصلاة ليس المراد به ما يقابل القضاء فإن التيمم بنية القضاء أيضا صحيح اتفاقا بل ما يشمله. [4]قوله خلافا لزفر له فإنه قال النية فيه ليست بفرض لأنه خلف عن الوضوء فكما لا تشترط فيه النية لا تشترط في التيمم أيضا وإلا تلزم مخالفة الخلف للأصل. وجوابه إنه لا بأس بذلك إذا دل دليل على مخالفة الخلف للأصل في بعض الأحكام.
With the intention of performing prayer. [3] He said: 'Performing prayer' – it does not mean what is opposite of make-up, for tayammum with the intention of make-up is also valid by agreement, rather it includes it. [4] He said: 'Contrary to Zufar', for he said: intention in it is not obligatory, because it is a substitute for wudu; so just as intention is not stipulated in wudu, it is not stipulated in tayammum either, otherwise it would entail the substitute differing from the original. And the answer is: There is no harm in that if evidence indicates that the substitute differs from the original in some rulings.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement of intention (niyyah) in tayammum. The matn includes the phrase 'with the intention of performing prayer', and the commentator clarifies that 'performing prayer' here includes both adā' (timely performance) and qaḍā' (make-up), for intention is required in both. The main ruling is that intention is obligatory (fard) in tayammum, contrary to Imam Zufar. Zufar argued by qiyas: since tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and wudu does not require intention (in the Hanafi school, intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard), then tayammum should not require intention either, otherwise the substitute would differ from the original. The commentator refutes this by stating that it is permissible for a substitute to differ from the original in some rulings when there is textual evidence to that effect. Here, the evidence is that the Quran and Sunnah specify that tayammum requires intention, while wudu does not. Thus, the Hanafi school maintains that intention is fard in tayammum, establishing a distinction from wudu.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform tayammum for purification or to perform a specific prayer.
خلف (khalaf): Substitute or replacement; tayammum is a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the majority of Hanafis require intention in tayammum despite it being a substitute for wudu?
A) Because the Quran explicitly mentions intention for tayammum.
B) Because wudu also requires intention in the Hanafi school.
C) Because the substitute can differ from the original when evidence supports it.
D) Because Zufar’s view was weaker.

Key Takeaway
Intention is fard in tayammum, even though tayammum is a substitute for wudu, because a substitute may differ from its original when there is evidence to do so.

Tayammum Without Dust: The Hanafi Intra-Dispute on Naq'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the necessity of dust in tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Abu Yusuf on tayammum without dust, and explain the Quranic evidence for each position.

Core Idea
Dust is not required for valid tayammum: the earth itself suffices.

Tayammum is a purification substitute for water, but what if there is no visible dust? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that tayammum is valid even without dust, while a narration from Abu Yusuf requires dust. This lesson unpacks the proofs from the Quran and clarifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested act and condition
The act is tayammum (dry ablution). The contested condition is the presence of dust (naq') — fine particles that rise from a surface. The question: is dust required for validity?
The base matn states tayammum is valid 'without dust', signaling the dispute.
2
State the two positions
State clearly: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that tayammum is valid without dust. Abu Yusuf, in one narration, holds that dust is required for validity (unless unable to use pure earth).
There is also a narration from Abu Yusuf agreeing with the majority; the stronger view is the majority.
3
Locate the proofs
Identify the two Quranic verses cited. For Abu Yusuf: Quran 5:6 '…wipe your faces and hands from it (minhu)' — the pronoun 'it' refers to earth, implying using a part, which requires dust. For the majority: Quran 4:43 '…perform tayammum with pure earth (sa'idan tayyiban)…' without 'minhu', indicating earth in general, not specifically dust.
Both verses are mutawatir in transmission (qat'i thubut) but their indication (dalala) is open to interpretation (zanni).
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each verse supports its position. The minority (Abu Yusuf) argues that 'minhu' necessitates taking a portion of earth, which is only possible with dust. The majority argues that 'sa'idan tayyiban' in 4:43 is unqualified, and dust is merely a form of earth; the verse does not require a separate dust source.
The commentary notes that dust is considered 'fine earth' (turab raqiq), thus it is already included in the sa'id.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: tayammum is valid without dust. This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah and favored by later authorities like al-Marghinani. The stronger narration from Abu Yusuf also agrees, making it the operative fatwa.
The practical consequence: tayammum on a smooth rock or a dusty floor is valid without needing to raise additional dust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة التيمم ولو بلا نقع وعليه مع قدرته على الصعيد بنية أداء الصلاة (ولو بلا نقع وعليه) : أي على النقع ، فلو كنس داراً، أو هدم حائطاً ، أو كال حنطة ، فأصابَ وجهَهُ وذراعيه غبارٌ لا يجزئه حتى يُمر يده عليه ، (مع قدرته على الصعيد" بنية أداء الصلاة) [١]قوله : ولو بلا نقع ؛ متعلق بالحجر أو بكل طاهر؛ أي ولو كان ذلك الطاهر بلا نقع - بالفتح - أي غبار، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد له في رواية، وفي رواية أخرى عنه، وهو قول أبي يوسف الله أنه لا يجوز بدون الغبار ؛ لقوله : (فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُم مِّنْهُ ) فإن الضمير راجع إلى التراب، فيقتضي ذلك استعمال جزء منه، ولا يتصور ذلك بدون الغبار ومَن لم يشترطه استند بقوله في موضع آخر : فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُم ) (۳) ، وفي المقامِ مباحث مذكورة في «السعاية»(۳). [٢]قوله : مع قدرته على الصعيد ؛ إنما ذكره نفياً لما روي عن أبي يوسف له أنه لا يجوز التيمم على الغبارِ نفسه إلا عند العجز عن الصعيد، والصحيح قولهما أنه يجوز به مطلقاً ; لأنّ الغبار تراب رقيق. كذا في «المحيط»(4).
Book of Purification: Tayammum. And (it is valid) without dust, and upon him, while able to use pure earth, with intention to perform prayer. (And without dust and upon him): meaning upon the dust. So if he swept a house, or demolished a wall, or winnowed wheat, and dust hit his face and forearms, it does not suffice him until he passes his hand over it. (While able to use pure earth with intention to perform prayer). [1] His saying: 'And without dust' is connected to 'stone' or to 'every pure thing'; meaning even if that pure thing is without dust – with fatha – i.e., dust. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, according to one narration from him, and in another narration from him, it is the statement of Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him – that it is not valid without dust, due to His statement: '...and wipe your faces and your hands from it' (Quran 5:6), for the pronoun refers to earth, necessitating the use of a part of it, and that is inconceivable without dust. And one who did not stipulate it relied on His statement in another place: '...and perform tayammum with pure earth and wipe your faces and your hands' (Quran 4:43). [2] His saying: 'while able to use pure earth' is mentioned to negate what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that tayammum is not valid on dust itself except when unable to use pure earth. The correct position according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that it is absolutely valid because dust is fine earth. So recorded in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of tayammum using dust (naq') without a separate earth source. The main text states that tayammum is valid even without dust, but the commentary notes an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, tayammum is valid using any pure substance that yields dust, even if the dust is not from a separate earth sample. Abu Yusuf, however, reportedly requires the presence of dust that can be separately utilized, citing the verse 'wipe your faces and your hands from it' (Quran 5:6), where 'it' refers to earth, implying that a portion of the earth must be used. The opposing view relies on the verse 'perform tayammum with pure earth' (Quran 4:43), which does not specify dust. The preferred position (al-sahih) according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that tayammum on dust itself is valid absolutely, as dust is fine earth.

Key Terms
نقع (naq'): Dust or fine particles that rise from a surface.
صعيد (sa'id): Pure earth; the surface of the earth, including soil, sand, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because dust is not a condition.
B) No, because a stone is not pure earth.
C) Only if the stone is from a pure source.
D) No, because there is no dust to transfer.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid with any pure earth, whether or not it produces dust; dust is not a separate condition in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Intention (Niyyah) in Tayammum – Dispute with Zufar
Ruling with proof and rebuttal of Zufar's view on niyyah in tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that intention is fard in tayammum and evaluate Zufar's counterargument using the principle that a substitute may differ from the original when evidence indicates.

Core Idea
Earth is not purifying by nature; intention transforms it, so niyyah is fard in tayammum.

In this passage, the commentator establishes that intention (niyyah) is obligatory in tayammum, contrary to the view of Zufar. Zufar argued that since tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and wudu does not require intention, tayammum should not require it either. The Hanafi response relies on the Qur'anic command and the inherent impurity of earth. We will walk through the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: intention is fard in tayammum. Note that this applies to both major and minor impurities.
The passage also mentions that one tayammum suffices for both impurities if intention covers both.
2
Identify Zufar's position and his proof
Zufar said intention is not fard because tayammum is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu, and wudu does not require intention.
His argument is based on qiyas: the substitute should mirror the original.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that a substitute may differ from the original when there is evidence (dalil). Here, the Qur'anic verse 'fa-tayammamu' linguistically implies intention (qasd). Also, earth is not naturally purifying; it becomes purifying only through intention, unlike water.
The key point: water is created purifying (tahur), earth is not.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a person performs tayammum without intention, according to the majority Hanafi view it is invalid; according to Zufar it is valid.
The mufta bihi is the majority view requiring intention.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on specification
If a person has both major and minor impurities, the correct view (from Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that intending wudu suffices for janabah; specification is not required.
This is contrary to the view of Abu Bakr al-Razi, who required specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالنِّيَّةُ فرضٌ في التيمم خلافا لزُفَرَ اللهُ ، حتى إذا كان به حدثان حدث يوجبُ الغُسل كالجنابة ، وحدث يوجب الوضوء ينبغي أن ينوي عنهما، فإن نَوَى عن أحدهما لا يقع عن الآخر، لكن يكفي تيمم واحد عنهما. [٤]قوله : خلافاً لزفر له ، فإنّه قال : النية فيه ليست بفرض ؛ لأنه خلف عن الوضوء، فكما لا تشترط فيه النية لا تشترط في التيمم أيضاً، وإلا تلزم مخالفة الخلف للأصل. وجوابه : إنّه لا بأس بذلك إذا دلّ دليل على مخالفة الخلف للأصل في بعض الأوصاف، وهو هاهنا موجود ؛ فإن قوله : فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا يدل على ذلك ; لأنّ التيمم في اللغةِ هوا القصد. ويؤيده أنّ التراب غير طهور في نفسه، بل هو ملوّث في نفسه، وإنما جُعِلَ طهوراً حال إرادة الصلاة فتشترط فيه النيّة (۳) ، بخلاف الماء فإنّه خُلق طهوراً فلا تشترط في التطهير به النية. [1] قوله : ينبغي أن ينوي عنهما ؛ أي عن الجنابة والحدث الأصغر، وفيه خلاف، فعند أبي بكر الرازي له من أصحابنا تجب في هذه الصورة نية التعيين والتمييز، وروى محمد بن سماعة له عن محمد الله أنَّ الجنب إذا تيمم يريد به الوضوء أجزأه عن الجنابة، وهو الصحيح كما في «الهداية وشروحها، فما ذكره الشارح هاهنا خلاف المذهب، إلا أن يحمل قوله : ينبغي على الاستحباب.
So intention is obligatory in tayammum contrary to Zufar. So if a person has two impurities – an impurity requiring ghusl like janabah and an impurity requiring wudu – he should intend both; for if he intends only one, it does not suffice for the other, but one tayammum suffices for both. [4] His saying: contrary to Zufar – he said that intention is not obligatory in it because it is a substitute for wudu, and just as intention is not required in wudu, it is not required in tayammum; otherwise there would be inconsistency of the substitute with the original. The answer: there is no harm if evidence indicates inconsistency of the substitute with the original in some attributes, and this is present here; for His statement: 'perform tayammum with pure earth' indicates this, because tayammum linguistically means intention. This is supported by the fact that earth is not purifying by nature, rather it is impure by nature, and it is made purifying only at the time of intending prayer, so intention is required in it, unlike water which is created purifying, so intention is not required for purification with it. [1] His saying: 'he should intend both' means for janabah and minor impurity; and there is disagreement. According to Abu Bakr al-Razi, among our companions, in this situation intention of specification and differentiation is obligatory. Muhammad ibn Samā'ah narrated from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) that if a junub person makes tayammum intending wudu, it suffices for janabah, and this is the correct view as in al-Hidayah and its commentaries. What the commentator mentioned here is contrary to the madhhab, unless his word 'should' is interpreted as recommended.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage establishes that intention (niyyah) is obligatory (fard) in tayammum, contrary to the opinion of Zufar, who argued that since tayammum is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu, and wudu does not require intention, tayammum should also not require it. The Hanafi response is that a substitute may differ from the original when there is evidence. Here, the Qur'anic verse 'perform tayammum' (fa-tayammamu) linguistically implies intention (qasd), and unlike water, earth is not naturally purifying but is made purifying by intention. The passage also discusses a practical case: a person with both junub and minor hadath should intend both impurities; if he intends only one, it does not suffice for the other. However, one tayammum is sufficient for both. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Bakr al-Razi requires specifying which impurity is intended, while the correct view (al-sahih) from Muhammad al-Shaybani is that if a junub person intends wudu, it suffices for janabah; thus explicit specification is not compulsory.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention to purify oneself for prayer or to remove ritual impurity.
خلف (khalaf): A substitute that replaces the original when the original is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require intention in tayammum but not in wudu?
A) Because water is purifying by nature, while earth is not.
B) Because tayammum is a supererogatory act.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly commands intention only for tayammum.
D) Because of a consensus among all scholars.

Key Takeaway
Intention is fard in tayammum because earth is not inherently purifying; the substitute can differ from the original when evidence supports.

Tayammum of a Disbeliever is Invalid
Ruling that a disbeliever's tayammum is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a disbeliever's tayammum and identify that Islam is a necessary condition for its validity.

Core Idea
Islam is a condition for tayammum; without it, tayammum is void even if intended for Islam.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key distinction: tayammum is not valid from a disbeliever, even if he intends to embrace Islam. The reason is that Islam itself is a prerequisite (shart) for this form of purification. Understanding this ruling prevents invalid acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
State the explicit ruling
The passage clearly states: 'The tayammum of a disbeliever for his Islam is not valid.' Identify the act (tayammum), the subject (kafir), and the ruling (invalid/batil).
Focus on the legal consequence: prayer after this tayammum is invalid.
2
Identify the condition (shart)
The text says the reason is that 'Islam is one of the conditions for its validity.' Therefore, Islam is a necessary condition (shart) for a valid tayammum.
Contrast with wudu, where Islam is not a condition for validity, only for acceptance.
3
Recognize the scope of the ruling
The commentary states the ruling applies 'whether he intends a specific act of worship that is only valid with purification or not.' So no intention can make a disbeliever's tayammum valid.
The ruling is absolute, without exceptions.
4
Understand the practical consequence
If a disbeliever in a state of impurity (hadath) performs tayammum and then prays, that prayer is invalid. He must embrace Islam and, if water is unavailable, perform tayammum again as a Muslim.
This highlights the importance of correct sequence: Islam comes before purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يجوز تيمم كافر لإسلامه (فلا يجوز تيمم كافر) لإسلامه) : أي لا يجوزُ الصَّلاةُ بهذا التّيمم، إذا كان به حدث، لأنه من شرائط صحته الإسلام، فلا يجوز تيمم الكافر سواء نوى عبادة مقصودة لا تصح إلا بالطهارة أو لا.
So the tayammum of a disbeliever for his Islam is not valid. (The tayammum of a disbeliever for his Islam): meaning prayer is not valid with this tayammum, if he is in a state of impurity, because one of the conditions for its validity is Islam. So the tayammum of a disbeliever is not valid, whether he intends a specific act of worship that is only valid with purification or not.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage states that a disbeliever's tayammum is invalid, even if he intends to become Muslim. The reason is that Islam is a condition (shart) for the validity of tayammum. Since tayammum is a form of purification intended for acts of worship that require purity, a disbeliever's tayammum is not recognized regardless of his intention. This differs from wudu, which a disbeliever can perform validly if he later accepts Islam? Actually, the commentary indicates that tayammum's conditions include Islam, so it is not accepted from a disbeliever. Therefore, if a disbeliever performs tayammum and then prays, his prayer is invalid.

Key Terms
كافر (kafir): A person who does not believe in Islam; who rejects the faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is a disbeliever's tayammum valid if he intends to become Muslim with it?
A) Yes, because intention is present.
B) No, because Islam is a condition for validity.
C) It depends on whether he performs it for prayer.
D) Yes, if he uses pure earth.

Key Takeaway
A disbeliever's tayammum is void because Islam is a necessary condition for its validity.
