Ruling on Tayammum of a Non-Muslim for His Islam
Explains ruling and proof that tayammum of a kafir is invalid for his Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a non-Muslim's tayammum and explain why intention (niyyah) is essential for its validity.

Core Idea
A non-Muslim's tayammum is invalid because it lacks the intention for an act of worship requiring purification.

This lesson examines a specific ruling regarding tayammum: a non-Muslim cannot perform tayammum for the purpose of his Islam or for prayer. The Hanafi school holds that tayammum requires a valid intention (niyyah) to perform an act of worship that demands purification, such as prayer. Since a non-Muslim's intention to become Muslim is not a valid intention for purification, his tayammum is invalid. The proof is derived from the Qur'anic verse on tayammum and the principle that earth is not inherently pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that a non-Muslim's tayammum is not permissible for his Islam, meaning prayer is not valid with that tayammum. Identify the act (tayammum by a non-Muslim) and its ruling (invalid/batil).
The ruling is absolute: tayammum performed before a valid conversion lacks the necessary intention.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites the Quranic verse 'so perform tayammum with clean earth' (4:43) and notes that the word 'tayammum' linguistically means 'intention'. Understand that the verse implies tayammum is only valid when one intends purity for prayer.
The dalil is naqli (Quran) supported by lughawi (linguistic) reasoning.
3
Understand the linguistic argument
The word tayammum in Arabic means 'intention' or 'aim'. The verse's command is directed at believers, indicating that tayammum is for those who already intend to perform an act of worship (prayer). A non-Muslim does not have this valid intention.
This linguistic connection strengthens the proof that niyyah is essential.
4
Contrast with water
The author contrasts earth with water: water is created pure (tahur) inherently, so intention is not required for purification with water. Earth is not inherently pure; it is made pure only when one intends to use it for purification. Hence, intention is a condition for tayammum.
This contrast clarifies why intention is uniquely required for tayammum but not for wudu with water.
5
Apply to the non-Muslim
Since the non-Muslim lacks a valid intention for an act of worship (his intention is to become Muslim, not to perform prayer), his tayammum is invalid. The prayer performed with such invalid tayammum is also invalid.
The ruling underscores that the invalidity is not due to disbelief per se but due to the absence of proper niyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(فلا يجوز تيمم كافر) لإسلامه) : أي لا يجوزُ الصَّلاةُ بهذا التّيمم، وهو هاهنا موجود ؛ فإن قوله: فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا يدل على ذلك ؛ لأنّ التيمم في اللغةِ هو القصد. ويؤيده أنّ التراب غير طهور في نفسه، بل هو ملوّث في نفسه، وإنما جُعِلَ طهوراً حال إرادة الصلاة فتشترط فيه النيّة (٣) ، بخلاف الماء فإنّه خُلق طهوراً فلا تشترط في التطهير به النية.
(The tayammum of a non-Muslim is not permissible) for his Islam: i.e., prayer is not permissible with this tayammum, and the description (of impermissibility) is present here; for His statement: 'so perform tayammum with clean earth' indicates that, because tayammum in language is intention. And it is supported that earth is not pure in itself, rather it is impure in itself, and it is only made pure at the time of intending prayer, so intention is required in it, unlike water, for it was created pure, so intention is not required in purification with it.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran. The author (the commentator) explains the ruling that a non-Muslim cannot perform tayammum for the purpose of becoming Muslim (i.e., to make his Islam valid through purification). The reason is that tayammum is only valid when it is performed with the intention of prayer or a similar act of worship that requires purification. A non-Muslim's intention to become Muslim is not a valid intention for tayammum, because tayammum is meant for those who are already Muslims and need to perform prayer. The proof is from the verse 'fas'amu sa'idan tayyiban' (O you who believe...), which implies that tayammum is for those who are in a state of needing purification for prayer. Additionally, the earth is not inherently pure; it is only considered pure when one intends to use it for purification. Therefore, intention (niyyah) is essential for tayammum. This contrasts with water, which is inherently pure and does not require intention for purification. Thus, a non-Muslim's tayammum is invalid because he lacks the proper intention for an act of worship that requires purification.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
نية (niyyah): Intention to perform an act of worship or purification; essential for tayammum according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the tayammum of a non-Muslim invalid for his Islam according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because earth is not pure for a non-Muslim.
B) Because the non-Muslim lacks valid intention (niyyah) for prayer or an act requiring purification.
C) Because the non-Muslim cannot perform any acts of worship.
D) Because the verse of tayammum is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The validity of tayammum hinges on having a valid intention for an act of worship that requires purification; a non-Muslim's tayammum lacks this thus is invalid.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Intention for Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on niyyah for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on niyyah in tayammum, explain their differences, and identify the mufta bihi (operative) ruling.

Core Idea
General intention in tayammum suffices; specifying the impurity type is not required in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This passage from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāyah addresses a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: when a person in major impurity (janabah) performs tayammum with the intention of wudu (minor impurity), does it remove the janabah? Three views emerge: Abu Bakr al-Razi demands specification, Abu Yusuf requires intention for an intended act of worship (qurbah maqsudah), and Imam Muhammad holds that general intention suffices. The commentator declares Muhammad's view as sahih, making it the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The scenario is a person in janabah who performs tayammum intending wudu (i.e., intending to remove minor impurity). The question is: does this tayammum remove the janabah and allow him to pray?
The scenario is the same for all three positions.
2
List the three Hanafi positions
Abu Bakr al-Razi: specification (ta'yin) of the type of impurity is obligatory (wajib). Abu Yusuf: intention for an intended act of worship (qurbah maqsudah) like prayer is required; intending a non-intended act like Islam does not suffice. Imam Muhammad: general intention for purification (e.g., for wudu) suffices for both janabah and minor impurity.
These are intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not across schools.
3
Note the epistemological weight
Imam Muhammad's view is from Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmitted works) and is explicitly declared 'sahih' in Al-Hidayah and its commentaries. This gives it priority over the other views.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the highest level of authority within the Hanafi school.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the mufta bihi, a person in janabah who does tayammum intending wudu can pray without repeating tayammum. Abu Bakr al-Razi would require him to redo tayammum with specification. Abu Yusuf would require him to redo tayammum if he intended a non-intended act.
This shows how the difference affects daily practice.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Imam Muhammad: general intention suffices, and specification is not required. This is the ruling fatwa is based on.
The commentator's phrase 'wa huwa al-sahih' confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1] قوله : ينبغي أن ينوي عنهما ؛ أي عن الجنابة والحدث الأصغر، وفيه خلاف، فعند أبي بكر الرازي له من أصحابنا تجب في هذه الصورة نية التعيين والتمييز، وروى محمد بن سماعة له عن محمد الله أنَّ الجنب إذا تيمم يريد به الوضوء أجزأه عن الجنابة ، وهو الصحيح كما في «الهداية وشروحها، فما ذكره الشارح هاهنا خلاف المذهب، إلا أن يحمل قوله : ينبغي على الاستحباب) ١ ] قوله : أي لا يجوز...الخ ؛ . ؛ لما كان ظاهر عبارة المتن كعبارة «الهداية» و«الجامع الصغير) . ) عدم صحة تيمم الكافر بقصد الإسلام مطلقاً حتى لا ينوب مقام الغسل الذي يؤمر به الكافر عند إسلامه، وليس كذلك، أشار الشارح إلى دفعه بأن المراد أن تيمم الكافر لإسلامه غير معتبر في حق جواز الصلاة لا مطلقاً. [١]قوله : فعنده ...الخ ؛ اعلم أنّ العبادات على نوعين : مقصودة وغير مقصودة. والمراد بالمقصودة في هذا البحث هي أن تكون مشروعة ابتداء تقرباً إلى الله من غير أن يكون تبعاً لغيرها، وبعبارة أخرى هي ما لا يجب في ضمن شيء آخر بالتبعية، وغير المقصودة بخلافه. فمن الأول الإسلام، وسجدة التلاوة، وسجدة الشكر، والصلوات الخمس، وصلوة الجنازة وغيرها. ونحوها. ومن الثاني : دخول المسجد، ومس المصحف، وردّ السلام، وقراءة الأذكار، ثم المقصودة منها ما لا يصح أو لا يحلّ بدون الطهارة كالصلوات، وسجدة التلاوة، ومنها ما يصح بدونها كالإسلام. إذا تمهد لك هذا فاعرف أن الشرط لصحة التيمم في نفسه هو نية ما قصده لأجله، سواء كان قربة مقصودة أو غيرها وهذا بالاتفاق. وأما في حق صحة جواز الصلاة به فاختلفوا فيه : فعند أبي يوسف له تشترط نيّة القربة المقصودة، وإن كانت تـصـح بـدون الطهارة، فلو تيمم كافر لإسلامه وأسلم جازَ له أداء الصلاة به، نعم لو تيمم الكافر بقصد أداء الصلاة، ثمّ أسلم لا تصح أداء الصلاة به؛ لكون تلك النية منه لغوا، صرح به في «النهاية».
[1] His saying: 'It is appropriate that he intend for both' – i.e., for major impurity (janabah) and minor impurity, and there is a difference of opinion on it. According to Abu Bakr al-Razi, one of our companions, in this case the intention of specification and distinction is obligatory. And Muhammad ibn Sam'a related from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) that if a person in janabah performs tayammum intending by it wudu, it suffices him from janabah, and that is the correct view as in Al-Hidayah and its commentaries. So what the commentator mentioned here is contrary to the madhhab, unless his saying 'it is appropriate' is interpreted as recommendation. [1] His saying: 'i.e., it is not permissible...' – because the apparent wording of the matn is like the wording of Al-Hidayah and Al-Jami' al-Saghir. That the tayammum of a non-Muslim for his Islam is absolutely invalid, so that it does not take the place of the ghusl which the non-Muslim is commanded to do at his Islam, but it is not so. The commentator indicated its refutation by [saying] that what is meant is that the tayammum of a non-Muslim for his Islam is not considered for the permissibility of prayer, not absolutely. [1] His saying: 'According to him...'; know that acts of worship are of two types: intended (maqsudah) and non-intended. What is meant by 'intended' in this discussion is that which is legislated initially as an approach to Allah, not being subsidiary to another. In other words, it is that which is not obligatory within something else by way of subordination, and non-intended is the opposite. From the first category are Islam, the prostration of recitation, the prostration of thanks, the five prayers, the funeral prayer, and others like them. From the second category are entering the mosque, touching the mushaf, returning greetings, reciting remembrances. Then among the intended ones are those that are not valid or permissible without purification, like prayers and the prostration of recitation, and among them are those that are valid without it, like Islam. Once this is established, know that the condition for the validity of tayammum in itself is intending that for which it is done, whether it is an intended act of worship or not, and this is by agreement. As for the validity of the permissibility of prayer with it, they differed about it: According to Abu Yusuf, the intention of an intended act of worship is required, even if it is valid without purification. So if a non-Muslim performs tayammum for his Islam and becomes Muslim, it is permissible for him to perform prayer with it. But if the non-Muslim performs tayammum intending to perform prayer, then becomes Muslim, it is not valid to perform prayer with it because that intention is void. This is explicitly stated in Al-Nihayah.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of intention (niyyah) for tayammum, specifically whether a person in a state of major impurity (janabah) who performs tayammum intending wudu (minor purification) is valid for removing janabah. The commentator begins by noting that the statement 'it is appropriate that he intend for both' refers to intending both janabah and minor impurity. Then he presents a disagreement: Abu Bakr al-Razi (a Hanafi scholar) holds that in this case, one must specify which state one is intending to purify from (ta'yin). On the other hand, Muhammad ibn Sam'a reports from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that if a person in janabah performs tayammum with the intention of wudu, it suffices for janabah as well. The commentator declares this latter view as 'sahih' (correct) based on Al-Hidayah and its commentaries, thus the view of the commentator (i.e., the sharh) is contrary to the relied-upon madhhab position unless his wording 'it is appropriate' is taken as recommendation (istihbab). The passage then goes into a classification of acts of worship into 'intended' (maqsudah) and 'non-intended'. Intended acts are those legislated as independent acts of obedience to Allah, like Islam, prayer, etc. Non-intended acts are those that are subsidiary, like entering the mosque. Within intended acts, some require purity (like prayer) and some do not (like Islam). Then the text explains the condition for the validity of tayammum: it requires intention for whichever purpose it is done, and this is agreed upon. However, when it comes to the permissibility of praying with that tayammum, there is a dispute. According to Abu Yusuf, the intention must be for an intended act of worship (qurbah maqsudah), even if that act itself is valid without purity (like Islam). So a kafir who does tayammum intending to become a Muslim can pray after Islam, but if he does tayammum intending to pray while still a kafir, it is invalid for prayer after Islam because the intention was void (since at that time he was not a Muslim capable of valid intention). The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that specification is not required, and tayammum with intention of wudu suffices for janabah.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): An intention that specifies which state of impurity (janabah or minor) one is purifying from.
قربة مقصودة (qurbah maqsudah): An act of worship legislated as an independent act of obedience to Allah, not as a subsidiary to another act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reliable Hanafi position (mufta bihi) in this passage, what is the ruling on a person in janabah who performs tayammum with the intention of wudu?
A) It is invalid; he must intend janabah specifically.
B) It is sufficient for both janabah and minor impurity.
C) It is only valid if he also intends to pray afterward.
D) It is valid only according to Abu Yusuf.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that tayammum with a general intention for purification suffices for both janabah and minor impurity without requiring specification.

Intention in Tayammum: The Dispute Between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intention for tayammum's validity for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the type of intention required for tayammum to be valid for prayer and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
For tayammum to permit prayer, the intention must be for a primary act that requires purification — not merely any act of worship.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary tackles a fascinating intra-madhhab dispute: can a person who performs tayammum with a specific intention — like embracing Islam or touching the Quran — then pray with that tayammum? The answer reveals a sophisticated classification of acts of worship and highlights how the Hanafi school refines its rulings through careful analysis of intention and purpose.

Guided Path
1
Classify acts of worship
The passage divides acts of worship into primary (qurba maqsuda) and subsidiary (qurba ghayr maqsuda). Primary acts are independent acts of drawing near to God; subsidiary acts are means to other ends. Among primary acts, some require purification (e.g., prayer) and some do not (e.g., embracing Islam).
This classification is key to understanding the dispute.
2
Identify the consensus
All three imams agree that for tayammum itself to be valid, any intention for whatever purpose suffices. The dispute is not about the tayammum's validity but about whether that tayammum can then be used to perform the obligatory prayer.
The consensus is on the basic validity of tayammum itself.
3
Locate the dispute
The disagreement concerns the intention required for tayammum to be valid for prayer. Abu Yusuf requires intention for any primary act of worship, even one that does not require purification. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require intention for a primary act that is not valid without purification.
This is the core of the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the rulings to examples
Work through the examples: a disbeliever's tayammum for Islam, tayammum for funeral prayer, for prostration of recitation, for touching the Quran, for entering a mosque. For each, determine whether prayer is valid according to each imam.
The thamarah al-khilaf is most clearly seen in the disbeliever example.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The commentary's detailed examples and rejection of Abu Yusuf's view confirm this. Later authoritative works (like al-Hidayah's commentaries) prefer this view.
For fatwa, the position of the two is operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة التيمم

عندهما، خلافاً لأبي يوسف : فعنده يشترط لصحة التيمم في حق جواز الصَّلاةِ أن ينوي قربة مقصودة، سواء كانت لا تصح بدون الطهارة كالصَّلاة، أو تصح كالإسلام.

الصغير) . ) عدم صحة تيمم الكافر بقصد الإسلام مطلقاً حتى لا ينوب مقام الغسل الذي يؤمر به الكافر عند إسلامه، وليس كذلك، أشار الشارح إلى دفعه بأن المراد أن تيمم الكافر لإسلامه غير معتبر في حق جواز الصلاة لا مطلقاً.

[١]قوله : فعنده ...الخ ؛ اعلم أنّ العبادات على نوعين : مقصودة وغير مقصودة. والمراد بالمقصودة في هذا البحث هي أن تكون مشروعة ابتداء تقرباً إلى الله من غير أن يكون تبعاً لغيرها، وبعبارة أخرى هي ما لا يجب في ضمن شيء آخر بالتبعية، وغير المقصودة بخلافه.

فمن الأول الإسلام، وسجدة التلاوة، وسجدة الشكر، والصلوات الخمس، وصلوة الجنازة وغيرها. ونحوها.

ومن الثاني : دخول المسجد، ومس المصحف، وردّ السلام، وقراءة الأذكار،

ثم المقصودة منها ما لا يصح أو لا يحلّ بدون الطهارة كالصلوات، وسجدة التلاوة، ومنها ما يصح بدونها كالإسلام. إذا تمهد لك هذا فاعرف أن الشرط لصحة التيمم في نفسه هو نية ما قصده لأجله، سواء كان قربة مقصودة أو غيرها وهذا بالاتفاق.

وأما في حق صحة جواز الصلاة به فاختلفوا فيه :

فعند أبي يوسف له تشترط نيّة القربة المقصودة، وإن كانت تـصـح بـدون الطهارة، فلو تيمم كافر لإسلامه وأسلم جازَ له أداء الصلاة به، نعم لو تيمم الكافر بقصد أداء الصلاة، ثمّ أسلم لا تصح أداء الصلاة به؛ لكون تلك النية منه لغوا، صرح به في «النهاية».

وعندهما: قربة مقصودة لا تصح إلا بالطهارة، فإن تيمم الصلاة الجنازة"، أو لسجدة التَّلاوةِ يجوزُ بهذا التّيمم أداء المكتوبات ، وإن تيمم لمس المصحف أو دخول المسجدِ لا تصح به الصَّلاة؛ لأنه لم ينو به قربة مقصودة"، لكن يحل له مس المصحف، ودخول المسجد.

وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد الله تشترط نيّة القرية المقصودة التي لا تصح بدون الطهارة، وإن شئت الاطلاع على دلائل القولين مع ما لها وما عليها فارجع إلى حواشي «الهداية»(۱).

[١] قوله : تيمم ... الخ ؛ أي عند العجز عن استعمال الماء، وأما عند القدرة فلا يجوز التيمم لسجدة التلاوة مطلقاً ؛ لأنها مما تشترط لها الطهارة، وما في «جامع الرموز ) من جواز التيمم لها مع القدرة على الماء فلا عبرة به.

[٢] قوله : لصلاة الجنازة؛ هذا محمول على ما إذا لم يكن واجداً للماء، أما إذا تيمم لها مع وجوده لخوف الفوت فإنّ تيمّمه يبطل لفراغه منها. كذا في البحر» (۳). [٣] قوله : لأنه لم ينو قربة مقصودة ؛ فإنّ مس المصحف لم يشرع عبادة إلا للقراءة، ودخول المسجد لم يكن عبادة إلا لما يؤدى فيه، وكذا لو تيمم لقراءة القرآن عن ظهر القلب أو المصحف أو لزيارة القبور أو لدفن الميت، أو لرد السلام، أو تعليم الغير لا يجوز له أداء الصلاة بهذا التيمم ؛ لأنها عبادات غير مقصودة. كذا في «فتاوى قاضي خان»(4).

[٤] قوله : لكن يحلّ له مس المصحف ودخول المسجد، هذا عند فقد الماء أو العجز عن استعماله، وأمّا عند القدرة عليه فلا يحل له مس المصحف ؛ لأنه مما يشترط له الطهارة، ويحلّ دخول المسجد بناءً على أنّ ما لا تشترط له الطهارة يكفي له التيمم مع القدرة على الماء، كما فصله في شرعة الإسلام»، وشرحه« مفتاح الجنان»، و«البزازية» وغيرها.
The Book of Purification: Tayammum

According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf: According to him (Abu Yusuf), for the validity of tayammum in respect of permitting prayer, it is required that one intend a primary act of worship, whether that act is not valid without purification like prayer, or is valid without it like Islam.

... [continued]
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqaya, discussing a crucial intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the intention required for tayammum to be valid for performing prayer. The author first clarifies that acts of worship are of two types: primary (maqsuda) and subsidiary (ghayr maqsuda). Primary acts are legislated as independent acts of drawing near to God, not as subordinates to other acts, such as Islam, prostration of recitation, prayer, etc. Subsidiary acts include entering a mosque, touching the Quran, responding to salams, and reciting dhikr. Among primary acts, some are not valid without purification (e.g., prayer), while others are valid without it (e.g., embracing Islam). By consensus, the condition for the validity of tayammum in itself is intention for whatever purpose one performs it, whether a primary or subsidiary act. However, the dispute arises concerning the validity of prayer performed with that tayammum. According to Abu Yusuf, the intention must be for a primary act of worship, even if that act is valid without purification (like Islam). Thus, if a disbeliever performs tayammum intending to embrace Islam and then embraces Islam, he may pray with that tayammum. But if he intended to pray while still a disbeliever, the prayer is not valid because that intention is void. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), the intention must be for a primary act of worship that is not valid without purification. So if one performs tayammum for the funeral prayer or for the prostration of recitation (which require purification), then obligatory prayers are valid with it. If one performs tayammum for touching the Quran or entering the mosque (subsidiary acts), prayer is not valid with that tayammum, though those acts become permissible. The text then discusses additional rulings: tayammum for prostration of recitation is only allowed when water is unavailable; tayammum for funeral prayer when water is available is invalid if done for fear of missing the prayer; and acts like reciting Quran from memory, visiting graves, etc., are subsidiary acts, so prayer is not valid with such tayammum. Finally, it clarifies that touching the Quran is not allowed when water is available because it requires purification, while entering the mosque is permissible even if one could have used water, since it is a subsidiary act that does not require purification for its permissibility.

Key Terms
قربة مقصودة (qurba maqsuda): A primary act of worship legislated as an independent means of drawing near to God, not as a subordinate to another act. Examples: obligatory prayers, prostration of recitation, Islam.
قربة غير مقصودة (qurba ghayr maqsuda): A subsidiary act of worship that is not an end in itself but is a means to something else, e.g., entering a mosque, touching the Quran, responding to salaam.
تيمم (tayammum): A dry ritual purification using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or its use is harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), if a person performs tayammum intending to touch the Quran (for reading), can he then perform the obligatory prayer with that tayammum?
A) Yes, because touching the Quran is an act of worship and any intention for worship suffices.
B) No, because touching the Quran is a subsidiary act that does not require purification, and tayammum for it does not permit prayer.
C) Yes, because tayammum is valid for any purpose and then all acts are permissible.
D) No, because touching the Quran is invalid without purification.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the validity of tayammum for prayer depends on the intention being for a primary act that requires purification; intention for subsidiary acts or acts valid without purification does not suffice.
